## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations & dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration determined by position x and velocity v, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillator: x' = v and v' = dv_dt = f(x, v, t). Common structures encode restoring forces from a potential (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (simple harmonic motion): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations about stable equilibrium)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper, near-linear regime)
- Constant-bias / shifted equilibrium: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) - c2 * v (equilibrium offset due to preload/gravity in linearized coordinates)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Pure nonlinear stiffness (odd polynomial restoring): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (strongly nonlinear conservative spring)
- Pendulum-type restoring torque: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations with viscous losses)
- Quadratic drag / nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag with restoring force)
- Coulomb/friction-like damping (smoothed sign): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (dry friction approximation without discontinuity)
- Rayleigh damping (self-excited/limit-cycle form): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent damping producing sustained oscillations)
- van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (limit cycles via position-dependent damping)
- Externally forced oscillator (harmonic drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven resonance response)
- Multi-harmonic/phase-shift forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (non-sinusoidal periodic excitation)
- Parametrically excited stiffness (Mathieu-like): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance via time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear resonance/chaos model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically appear as functions of x only and are odd around equilibrium (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)), reflecting symmetry of many oscillators.
- Damping terms are typically odd in v (e.g., v, v*Abs(v), tanh(c*v)), ensuring dissipation opposes the direction of motion.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is often indicated by the sign of an x**3 term in dv_dt (Duffing): it shifts resonance frequency with amplitude.
- Limit cycles/self-excited oscillations often arise from negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, captured by (c0 - c1*v**2)*v or (1 - c*x**2)*v structures.
- External periodic forcing appears as additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; the forcing frequency parameters govern resonance bands and entrainment.
- Parametric excitation is suggested by multiplicative time-dependence on x (e.g., x*cos(c*t)), distinguishing it from additive forcing and indicating Mathieu-type instability regions.
- Large-angle pendulum behavior is suggested when linear x is replaced by sin(c*x); this introduces amplitude-dependent period without needing polynomial terms.
- Velocity-squared drag (v*Abs(v)) is a hallmark of turbulent/aerodynamic losses, producing faster decay at high speeds than linear damping.
- Equilibrium shifts or constant loads can be represented by using (x - c) inside restoring terms, implying the system oscillates about a nonzero mean position.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO35)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*Abs(v)**c1 + c2)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
-3.4278620084\,x\,(0.034997753689396\,|v|^{1/3}+1)\;+\;0.100299255716928\sin(t)\;-\;0.888494670723871\sin(v)
\]
So GT is the sum of three *structurally essential* parts:

1) a \(t\)-only sinusoid: \(A\sin(t)\) with \(A\neq 0\)  
2) a \(v\)-only sinusoid: \(B\sin(v)\) with \(B\neq 0\)  
3) an \(x\)-linear term whose coefficient depends on \(|v|^{1/3}\): \(-Kx(1+\alpha |v|^{1/3})\) with \(K\neq 0,\alpha\neq 0\)

Key consequence: any matching candidate must be able to produce **both** \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(v)\) terms, and must be able to produce an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) coupling (with absolute value) in addition to an \(x\) term.

---

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

For all candidates 1–33 and 36–50:
- They include at most trigonometric functions of **t** (sin/cos of linear t), but **none contains \(\sin(v)\)** or any trig function of \(v\).
- Many include polynomial/rational/log/exp/tanh in \(v\), but those cannot be made identically equal to \(\sin(v)\) for all real \(v\) by choosing constants (different functional families; no parameter choice turns a polynomial/log/exp/tanh into a sine globally).
Therefore, **all of these fail** immediately because GT has the nonzero term \(-0.88849\sin(v)\).

I’ll still note the other structural mismatch that would remain even if \(\sin(v)\) were absent: GT needs an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term. Candidates offer couplings like \(v^2x\), \(vx\), \(x(c+v)^2\), \(t(c+v)^{c9}\), etc., but **none offers \(|v|^{1/3}x\)** (with Abs) except candidate 35 has a cube-root power but without Abs and with a shift.

Now the only candidates that even mention a \(1/3\) power are 35 and 45 (and 34 has power 3, not 1/3). Check those more carefully:

#### 34. \(c0*x + c1*tanh(c2*v) + c3*x**c4 + c5*sin(c6 + c7*t) + c8*x*(c9 + v)**3\)
- Has \(\sin(\text{affine in }t)\) so can match \(0.100299\sin(t)\) via phase/frequency: set \(c7=1\), \(c6=0\), \(c5=0.100299...\).
- But \(v\)-dependence is \(tanh(c2 v)\) and polynomial \((c9+v)^3\) coupled to \(x\), not \(\sin(v)\), and not \(|v|^{1/3}\).
- Cannot produce \(\sin(v)\). Fail.

#### 35. \(c0*x + c1*tanh(c2*v) + c3*sin(c4 + c5*t) + c6*v*x + c7*x*(c8 + v)**(1/3)\)
- Can match the \(t\)-sinusoid: choose \(c5=1\), \(c4=0\), \(c3=0.100299...\).
- Needs \(-0.88849\sin(v)\): candidate has only \(tanh(c2 v)\) as a pure \(v\)-only nonlinear term. No choice of constants makes \(tanh(c2 v)\equiv \sin(v)\) for all real \(v\). (Different analyticity/periodicity; tanh is monotone and bounded with limits ±1, sine is periodic.)
- Even ignoring that, the \(x\)-coupling term is \(x(c8+v)^{1/3}\) plus \(v x\). GT requires \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and also an \(x\) term. You could set \(c6=0\) and try \(c8=0\) to get \(x v^{1/3}\), but:
  - \(v^{1/3}\) (real cube root) equals \(\operatorname{sgn}(v)|v|^{1/3}\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). Because the domain includes negative \(v\), \(v^{1/3}\neq |v|^{1/3}\) globally.
  - No Abs is present, and no combination of the other terms can “flip” the sign only for negative \(v\) to convert \(v^{1/3}\) into \(|v|^{1/3}\).
- So it fails on both the missing \(\sin(v)\) and the Abs requirement. Fail.

#### 45. \(c0*x + c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*v**3 + c5*v + c6*cos(t) + c7*v*(c8 + x)**(1/3)\)
- Has only trig in \(t\), not in \(v\) ⇒ cannot produce \(\sin(v)\). Fail.
- Also its coupling is \(v(x+c8)^{1/3}\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Fail anyway.

All remaining candidates (1–33, 36–44, 46–50) similarly:
- Can match \(0.100299\sin(t)\) using \(c1\sin(c2 t+c3)\) and/or \(c7\cos(t)\) by phase shift (e.g., set cosine coefficient 0, set \(c2=1,c3=0,c1=0.100299\)).
- But **none contains \(\sin(v)\)**, and none contains an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term with Abs. Hence they cannot be globally equivalent to GT.

---

**Conclusion:** No candidate can reproduce the essential \(-0.88849\sin(v)\) term (and also none can reproduce the \(|v|^{1/3}x\) dependence with Abs).  
[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO35)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*Abs(v)**c1 + c2)*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-3.42786200841899*x*(0.034997753689396*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) + 0.100299255716928*sin(t) - 0.888494670723871*sin(v)`

Expanding the GT:
`-3.42786200841899*x - 0.119969938498498*x*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 0.100299255716928*sin(t) - 0.888494670723871*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions/terms:
1. `x` (linear in x)
2. `x * |v|^(1/3)` (product of x and |v|^(1/3))
3. `sin(t)` 
4. `sin(v)`

Key observations:
- The GT contains `sin(v)`, not polynomial terms in v
- The GT contains `x*|v|^(1/3)`, involving absolute value
- The GT contains `sin(t)` (which can be written as `sin(1*t + 0)`)
- No `cos(t)` term, no `v^3`, no `v` linear term, no `v^2*x`, no `log` terms

Now let me check each candidate. Most candidates contain terms like `v**3`, `v`, `cos(t)`, `v**2*x`, `v*x`, `log(...)`, etc. The critical question is whether any candidate can reproduce `sin(v)` and `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

**sin(v):** This is a transcendental function of v. No polynomial in v (like `c*v + c*v^3`) can equal `sin(v)` for all v. Similarly, `tanh(v)`, `log(v+1)`, `v^c` cannot equal `sin(v)`.

**x*|v|^(1/3):** This requires a term coupling x and a fractional power of |v|. Terms like `v^2*x`, `v*x`, `x*(c+v)^2`, `x*(c+v)^(1/3)` are different.

Let me scan all candidates for the presence of `sin(v)`:
- None of the 50 candidates contain `sin(v)`.

Since `sin(v)` with coefficient `-0.8885` is a required term in the GT, and `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, logarithmic, and other basis functions present in the candidates, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify there's no hidden way to produce `sin(v)`: The candidates use `sin(c*t + c)`, `cos(t)`, `tanh(c*v)`, `log(c*v+1)`, `v^c`, polynomial terms in v, etc. None of these can produce `sin(v)` since v and t are independent variables, and sin(v) cannot be expressed as any combination of the basis functions present.
